--- Commit Message ---
LU-12043 llite: improve single-thread read performance

Here is whole history:

Currently, for sequential read IO, We grow up window
size very quickly, and once we cached @max_readahead_per_file
pages. For following command:

  dd if=/mnt/lustre/file of=/dev/null bs=1M

We will do something like following:
...
64M bytes cached.
fast io for 16M bytes
readahead extra 16M to fill up window.
fast io for 16M bytes
readahead extra 16M to fill up window.
....

In this way, we could only use fast IO for 16M bytes and
then fall through non-fast IO mode. this is also reason
that why increasing @max_readahead_per_file don't give us
performances up, since this value only changes how much
memory we cached in memory, during my testing whatever
I changed the value, i could only get 2GB/s for single thread
read.

Actually, we could do this better, if we have used
more than 16M bytes readahead pages, submit another readahead
requests in the background. and ideally, we could always
use fast IO.

Test							Patched		Unpatched
dd if=file of=/dev/null bs=1M.	 			4.0G/s		1.9G/s
ior -np 192 r -t 1m -b 4g -F -e -vv -o /cache1/ior -k	11195.97	10817.02 MB/sec

Tested with drop OSS and client memory before every run.
max_readahead_per_mb=128M, RPC size is 16M.
dd file's size is 400G which is double of memory or so.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2019-03-06 13:53:19.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2:

James,

What is your intent with "schedule_work_on"?  Because I don't really like tightly binding work like this.  Daemons are a different matter, since they're long lived, but if we're spawning threads to do this work each time, with a work queue, shouldn't we let the scheduler handle where they run...?

And yes, we should figure out how to respect the CPT table as well.  Presumably it's possible to restrict a workqueue to a mask of CPUs?

And maybe a possible number of threads in the work queue is just NUMCPUs?  Or 1/4 NUMCPUs, maybe, to be more conservative?  This would be good to have as a tunable so sites can tweak it.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2019-03-06 16:59:57.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2:

One high-level design comment - running multiple threads can improve single-threaded read performance, but it could hurt the very common thread-per-core performance due to too many threads.

That means we also need to run the standard thread-per-core IOR benchmarks to get an idea of how much this affects performance there, instead of only single-thread-per-node performance.

The ptlrpcd code handles this problem by having a work queue per core (I _think_ it is also managed by CPT), and ptlrpcd does "work stealing" from other ptlrpcds if the local ptlrpc has no work.  That keeps operations on the local cores if there is a multi-threaded workload, but allows parallel operations if there are fewer threads than ptlrpcd.

--- Message (Wang Shilong, 2019-03-06 17:30:03.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2:

btw, the main reason that patch improve performance comes from async thread to push forward
fast IO as much as possible.

For example, for our testing ,we use 16M RPC, actually only one backaround thread running for
the test.

Anyway, let's check thread-per-core IOR benchmarks, thanks for pointing this out!

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2019-03-06 18:19:55.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2:

Yes, of course - the background thread pulls in data allowing the user thread to read more from the page cache.

I have a few concerns.
1. When the user thread tries to read pages that are selected for readahead in the worker thread, what happens?  Does it just wait?  (This is probably best)
2. What happens with multiple threads reading the same file?  I am concerned that maybe there is a pattern that would cause us to thrash, submitting the same blocks of data over and over for readahead...?  Just wondering

--- Message (Wang Shilong, 2019-03-06 19:14:03.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2:

Hi Patrick,

As far as my understanding,

For the question 1, Readahead detection call it miss inside window, in this case Readahead window will be reset to 0, so I think it doesn't wait, this is true with or without patch.

For the question 2, I guess most of cases, this will be detected as random read which won't
submit readahead again and again.

But yeah, it will be nice to be run some test with your concerns.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2019-03-06 19:23:21.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2:

One idea that has been discussed in LU-11416, but may be worthwhile to mention here for a follow-on patch, is for files that are accessed randomly, but can fit easily into RAM we should consider doing readahead for the whole file.

--- Message (Wang Shilong, 2019-03-06 19:23:37.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2:

One of the main point that this patch might be affected is that async workers dosn't pull pages into memory when users want to read those pages, this will make Read miss inside window happen which means we will reset readahead window, this won't happen before since it wait before read finish before.

I think this case could happen in the following cases with this patch:

This client IO load is high or @max_readahead_page_per_file is small for example less than
16M which we should disable async readahead.

For the first case if system is super busy, I think it fine to reset readahead window? or
we could add an interface to disable readahead.

--- Message (Wang Shilong, 2019-03-06 19:29:30.000000000) ---
Patch Set 2:

 > accessed randomly, but can fit easily into RAM we should consider
 > doing readahead for the whole file.

random read, will follow on it.

Patch Set 25:

> As discussed with Jinshan,

Hmm...This sounds like an *advanced optimization*, I don't think this condition is problem, since we can disable async RA on demand. IMO, it's better to postpone the *optimization* if we hit real similar problem, it won't be late then.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2019-04-25 11:28:58.000000000) ---
Patch Set 25:

I haven't reviewed the patch yet, but it is already providing enough benefit that it should be landed sooner instead of later. We can't do further optimization in a separated patch.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2019-04-25 17:27:01.000000000) ---
Patch Set 25:

Yeah, I agree with Andreas and Zheng:
I think even if the CPUs are busy, handing them readahead work to do is reasonable.  The readahead is not 'extra' work (except for scheduling overhead, etc), it is real work that they will do now or later.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2019-04-25 17:30:16.000000000) ---
Patch Set 25:

And, yes, it's not perfect, but I don't think it will be a big problem.  And if it is, users can turn this off and we can fix it later.  (Also, we will know better what the real problem is, instead of trying to guess what might happen.)

I will try to review current version soon; I don't think it needs scheduling related changes.

--- Message (Patrick Farrell, 2019-04-25 17:35:16.000000000) ---
Patch Set 25:

BTW, I think the main concern people might have is scheduler noise...  But I don't think that would be helped much by something as simple as noticing when the system is busy, I think?

I am curious about Jinshan's suggestion to try doing more readahead in the same context.  If you haven't, maybe you can try that and see if it goes even faster (or just as fast but with less CPU usage)?  One of the problems with the old pio write work was how long it took to start the worker threads, etc.  (Although that was synchronous, not async, so it was worse.)

But I don't want to hold this patch up too much for optimizations either.  The current version is very good already.

--- Message (Wang Shilong, 2019-04-26 00:31:28.000000000) ---
Patch Set 25:

> BTW, I think the main concern people might have is scheduler
 > noise...  But I don't think that would be helped much by something
 > as simple as noticing when the system is busy, I think?
 > 
 > I am curious about Jinshan's suggestion to try doing more readahead
 > in the same context.  If you haven't, maybe you can try that and
 > see if it goes even faster (or just as fast but with less CPU

By doing more readahead inside current IO context
might help, but won't help much, just considering our testing that
increase @max_readahead_per_file won't help much for read performance.

The key point is we should use fast read as much as possible, and avoid
latency of triggered IO in the context is the bottleneck we could not reach more
than 2GB/s currently.
